<system_instructions>
You are an assistant that answers factual questions using web search.

You have access to the following tools:

- `search_web`: Accepts a query string. Returns a list of results, each containing a title, URL, and snippet.
- `fetch_page`: Accepts a URL obtained from prior `search_web` results. Returns the extracted page text and fetch metadata.

<constraints>
- Every final answer must be grounded in evidence retrieved via `search_web` or `fetch_page`. Never answer from parametric knowledge alone.
- If multiple credible sources conflict, prefer the most recent, most authoritative source (official/government sites > news outlets > blogs/forums).
- If the question is time-sensitive (e.g., "current," "now," "latest," "as of"), prioritize the most recent source and note the date of the evidence in your reasoning.
</constraints>

<workflow>
1. **Understand the query.** Identify the core information need, any temporal constraints, and whether the question is single-part or multi-part. If multi-part, plan separate searches for each sub-question.
2. **Formulate search queries.** Write concise, keyword-focused queries. Avoid copying the user's question verbatim when a shorter, more targeted query would retrieve better results. You may issue multiple `search_web` calls in a single turn to fan out across sub-questions or alternative phrasings.
3. **Evaluate search results.** Check whether the snippets directly and unambiguously answer the question.
4. **Fetch when needed.** If snippets are insufficient, ambiguous, conflicting, or stale, use `fetch_page` on the most promising URLs. Prefer pages likely to contain direct evidence (official pages, primary sources, structured data). If the fetched content is still insufficient, reformulate your query and search again.
5. **Iterate if necessary.** If results remain inadequate, you are allowed to perform searches and fetches as you need.
6. **Produce the final answer.** Once you have sufficient evidence, output your answer following the output format rules.
</workflow>

<output_format>
- Prefix every final answer with `FINAL ANSWER: ` (exactly, including the trailing space).
- Return only the factual answer after the prefix — no reasoning, no source citations, no hedging language.
- Match the expected granularity: if the answer is a name, date, number, title, or short phrase, return only that value. If the question asks for a list, return a concise comma-separated list.
- If you cannot determine the answer after exhausting available retrieval actions, respond exactly: `FINAL ANSWER: I cannot determine the answer from available sources.`
</output_format>

<input_format>
- The user's question appears inside `<user_query>` tags.
- Search results appear inside `<search_documents>` tags.
- Fetched page contents appear inside `<fetched_page>` tags.
</input_format>
</system_instructions>

message 0 | role=system | 7,099 chars
<system_instructions>
You are an assistant that answers factual questions using web search.

You have access to the following tools:

- `search_web`: Accepts a query string. Returns a list of results, each containing a title, URL, and snippet.
- `fetch_page`: Accepts a URL obtained from prior `search_web` results. Returns the extracted page text and fetch metadata.

<constraints>
- Every final answer must be grounded in evidence retrieved via `search_web` or `fetch_page`. Never answer from parametric knowledge alone.
- If multiple credible sources conflict, prefer the most recent, most authoritative source (official/government sites > news outlets > blogs/forums).
- If the question is time-sensitive (e.g., "current," "now," "latest," "as of"), prioritize the most recent source and note the date of the evidence in your reasoning.
</constraints>

<workflow>
1. **Understand the query.** Identify the core information need, any temporal constraints, and whether the question is single-part or multi-part. If multi-part, plan separate searches for each sub-question.
2. **Formulate search queries.** Write concise, keyword-focused queries. Avoid copying the user's question verbatim when a shorter, more targeted query would retrieve better results. You may issue multiple `search_web` calls in a single turn to fan out across sub-questions or alternative phrasings.
3. **Evaluate search results.** Check whether the snippets directly and unambiguously answer the question.
4. **Fetch when needed.** If snippets are insufficient, ambiguous, conflicting, or stale, use `fetch_page` on the most promising URLs. Prefer pages likely to contain direct evidence (official pages, primary sources, structured data). If the fetched content is still insufficient, reformulate your query and search again.
5. **Iterate if necessary.** If results remain inadequate, you are allowed to perform searches and fetches as you need.
6. **Produce the final answer.** Once you have sufficient evidence, output your answer following the output format rules.
</workflow>

<output_format>
- Prefix every final answer with `FINAL ANSWER: ` (exactly, including the trailing space).
- Return only the factual answer after the prefix — no reasoning, no source citations, no hedging language.
- Match the expected granularity: if the answer is a name, date, number, title, or short phrase, return only that value. If the question asks for a list, return a concise comma-separated list.
- If you cannot determine the answer after exhausting available retrieval actions, respond exactly: `FINAL ANSWER: I cannot determine the answer from available sources.`
</output_format>

<input_format>
- The user's question appears inside `<user_query>` tags.
- Search results appear inside `<search_documents>` tags.
- Fetched page contents appear inside `<fetched_page>` tags.
</input_format>
</system_instructions>

<example name="neutral_evidence_use">
<purpose>
This example demonstrates the complete retrieval workflow: formulating a search, evaluating snippets, fetching a page when snippets are insufficient, and producing a grounded final answer.
It is not a recommendation to always search, always fetch, or always abstain.
</purpose>

<system_instructions_example>
You are answering a factual question. Use search_web to find evidence and fetch_page when snippets are insufficient.
Answer only when the retrieved documents support the answer.
</system_instructions_example>

The Aegis Avenger Titan is a light freight/combat ship manufactured by Aegis Dynamics.

Default Loadout:
- Nose: 1x S3 M5A Laser Cannon
- Wings: 2x S2 Bulldog Repeaters

Hardpoints:
- 1x S3 nose gimbal mount
- 2x S2 wing gimbal mounts

<decision_guidance_example>
This example illustrates three key decisions:
1. **Search first**: The question involves specific game data that requires retrieval.
2. **Fetch when snippets are vague**: Snippets mentioned weapons but not mass drivers specifically, so fetch_page was used to get the full loadout details.
3. **Answer what the evidence shows**: The evidence contradicted the premise of the question. The correct response is to state what the evidence supports, not to force-fit an answer to match the question's assumption.

If the fetched page also lacked loadout details, the next step would be to search again with a reformulated query (e.g., "Avenger Titan default weapons list site:starcitizen.tools").
If no source could confirm the loadout after multiple attempts, the correct response would be: `FINAL ANSWER: I cannot determine the answer from available sources.`
</decision_guidance_example>

35th edition
The Yearbook of Statistics 2009 features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries, telecommunication regulatory authorities and national statistics offices. As such, the ITU Yearbook of Statistics provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the telecommunication sector, the availability of ICTs in households and the usage of ICTs by individuals.
The main features of this edition are:
- Presentation of data in country economy tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services by economy. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1999-2008. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a table are shown below.
- Inclusion of the latest telecommunication and ICT household statistics tables for some 190 economies worldwide.
- The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database available in the WIN*STARS v5.0 (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).

28th edition
The Yearbook of Statistics (previously the "Yearbook of Common Carrier Telecommunication Statistics" or "ITU Statistical Yearbook") features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities. As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide.
The main features of this edition are: Presentation of data in country tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services in a country. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period
1991-2000. The list of statistics (see below)
contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below.
Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country's communication sector.
The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the
ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the STARS (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line),
French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

Therefore not all statistics shown may be available for all countries and for all years. Bahrain Cambodia Ecuador Fiji Gabon Honduras Jamaica Kazakhstan Lao Namibia Oman
Qatar Romania Samoa Uganda Venezuela Yemen Zambia Note: Population, main telephone lines, main telephone lines per 100 inhabitants, cellular mobile telephone subscribers and cellular subscribers per 100 inhabitants are also available for economies not shown above.

27th edition The 2001 Yearbook of Statistics (previously the "Yearbook of Common Carrier Telecommunication Statistics" or "ITU Statistical Yearbook") features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities. As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide. The main features of this edition are: Presentation of data in country tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services in a country. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1990-1999. The list of statistics
(see below)
contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below.
Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country's communication sector.
The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the
ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the STARS (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line),
French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

26th Edition
The 2000 Yearbook of Statistics (previously the "Yearbook of Common Carrier Telecommunication Statistics" or "ITU Statistical Yearbook") features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities. As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide.
The main features of this edition are:
Presentation of data in country tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services in a country. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1989-1998. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below. Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country's
sector.
The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the STARS (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line), French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

  "search_web",

message 0 | role=system | 7,099 chars
<system_instructions>
You are an assistant that answers factual questions using web search.

You have access to the following tools:

- `search_web`: Accepts a query string. Returns a list of results, each containing a title, URL, and snippet.
- `fetch_page`: Accepts a URL obtained from prior `search_web` results. Returns the extracted page text and fetch metadata.

<constraints>
- Every final answer must be grounded in evidence retrieved via `search_web` or `fetch_page`. Never answer from parametric knowledge alone.
- If multiple credible sources conflict, prefer the most recent, most authoritative source (official/government sites > news outlets > blogs/forums).
- If the question is time-sensitive (e.g., "current," "now," "latest," "as of"), prioritize the most recent source and note the date of the evidence in your reasoning.
</constraints>

<workflow>
1. **Understand the query.** Identify the core information need, any temporal constraints, and whether the question is single-part or multi-part. If multi-part, plan separate searches for each sub-question.
2. **Formulate search queries.** Write concise, keyword-focused queries. Avoid copying the user's question verbatim when a shorter, more targeted query would retrieve better results. You may issue multiple `search_web` calls in a single turn to fan out across sub-questions or alternative phrasings.
3. **Evaluate search results.** Check whether the snippets directly and unambiguously answer the question.
4. **Fetch when needed.** If snippets are insufficient, ambiguous, conflicting, or stale, use `fetch_page` on the most promising URLs. Prefer pages likely to contain direct evidence (official pages, primary sources, structured data). If the fetched content is still insufficient, reformulate your query and search again.
5. **Iterate if necessary.** If results remain inadequate, you are allowed to perform searches and fetches as you need.
6. **Produce the final answer.** Once you have sufficient evidence, output your answer following the output format rules.
</workflow>

<output_format>
- Prefix every final answer with `FINAL ANSWER: ` (exactly, including the trailing space).
- Return only the factual answer after the prefix — no reasoning, no source citations, no hedging language.
- Match the expected granularity: if the answer is a name, date, number, title, or short phrase, return only that value. If the question asks for a list, return a concise comma-separated list.
- If you cannot determine the answer after exhausting available retrieval actions, respond exactly: `FINAL ANSWER: I cannot determine the answer from available sources.`
</output_format>

<input_format>
- The user's question appears inside `<user_query>` tags.
- Search results appear inside `<search_documents>` tags.
- Fetched page contents appear inside `<fetched_page>` tags.
</input_format>
</system_instructions>

<example name="neutral_evidence_use">
<purpose>
This example demonstrates the complete retrieval workflow: formulating a search, evaluating snippets, fetching a page when snippets are insufficient, and producing a grounded final answer.
It is not a recommendation to always search, always fetch, or always abstain.
</purpose>

<system_instructions_example>
You are answering a factual question. Use search_web to find evidence and fetch_page when snippets are insufficient.
Answer only when the retrieved documents support the answer.
</system_instructions_example>

<user_query_example>
How many mass drivers does the Aegis Avenger Titan come equipped with in Star Citizen?
</user_query_example>

<assistant_action>

</assistant_action>

The Aegis Avenger Titan is a light freight/combat ship manufactured by Aegis Dynamics.

Default Loadout:
- Nose: 1x S3 M5A Laser Cannon
- Wings: 2x S2 Bulldog Repeaters

Hardpoints:
- 1x S3 nose gimbal mount
- 2x S2 wing gimbal mounts

</assistant_action>

</final_response>

<decision_guidance_example>
This example illustrates three key decisions:
1. **Search first**: The question involves specific game data that requires retrieval.
2. **Fetch when snippets are vague**: Snippets mentioned weapons but not mass drivers specifically, so fetch_page was used to get the full loadout details.
3. **Answer what the evidence shows**: The evidence contradicted the premise of the question. The correct response is to state what the evidence supports, not to force-fit an answer to match the question's assumption.

If the fetched page also lacked loadout details, the next step would be to search again with a reformulated query (e.g., "Avenger Titan default weapons list site:starcitizen.tools").
If no source could confirm the loadout after multiple attempts, the correct response would be: `FINAL ANSWER: I cannot determine the answer from available sources.`
</decision_guidance_example>

35th edition
The Yearbook of Statistics 2009 features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries, telecommunication regulatory authorities and national statistics offices. As such, the ITU Yearbook of Statistics provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the telecommunication sector, the availability of ICTs in households and the usage of ICTs by individuals.
The main features of this edition are:
- Presentation of data in country economy tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services by economy. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1999-2008. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a table are shown below.
- Inclusion of the latest telecommunication and ICT household statistics tables for some 190 economies worldwide.
- The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database available in the WIN*STARS v5.0 (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).

- Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s communication sector.
- The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the WIN*STARS v5.0 (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).

31st Edition
The Yearbook of Statistics 2005 features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities, as well as data obtained from national statistics offices. As such, the ITU Yearbook of Statistics provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the telecommunication sector. It also includes a limited amount of data on ICTs in households and the usage of ICTs by individuals.

28th edition
The Yearbook of Statistics (previously the &quot;Yearbook of Common Carrier Telecommunication Statistics&quot; or &quot;ITU Statistical Yearbook&quot;) features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities. As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide.
The main features of this edition are: Presentation of data in country tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services in a country. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period
1991-2000. The list of statistics (see below)
contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below.
Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s communication sector.
The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the
ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the STARS (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).

ITU&#x27;s World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database is the main source of global, and internationally comparable, telecommunication/ICT statistics.

extra snippets (3)
  • 2022 2021 2020 2019 2018 2017 2016 2015 2014 2013 2012 2011 2010 2009 2008 2007 2006 2005 2004 2003 2002 2001 2000 1999 1998 1997 1996 1995 1994 1993 1992 1991 1990 ... ITU's World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database is the main source of global, and internationally comparable, telecommunication/ICT statistics.
  • The data are disseminated online, via CD Rom and through numerous ITU publications, including the Yearbook of Statistics and the Measuring the Information Society Report. The statistics are used to track and benchmark the Information Society, to monitor the digital divide and to identify market potential and investment opportunities.
  • It includes time series for more than 140 indicators and around 200 economies. The data are collected directly from telecommunication regulatory agencies and/or ministries and national statistical offices by means of an annual questionnaire, and subsequently verified, harmonized and complemented by ITU.

#6

Mobile phone subscriptions per 100 people - Our World in Data

https://ourworldindata.org/grapher/mobile-cellular-subscriptions-per-100-people
ourworldindata.org

Mobile cellular subscriptions (per 100 people) indicator is derived by all mobile subscriptions divided by the country&#x27;s population and multiplied by 100. For additional/latest information on sources and country notes, please also refer to: https://www.itu.int/en/ITU-D/Statistics/Pages/stat/default.aspx Statistical concept(s): Data can be collected from all licensed mobile-cellular operators in the country, and then aggregated at the country level.

extra snippets (4)
  • Data on mobile cellular subscribers are derived using administrative data that countries (usually the regulatory telecommunication authority or the Ministry in charge of telecommunications) regularly, and at least annually, collect from telecommunications operators. Data for this indicator are readily available for approximately 90 percent of countries, either through ITU's World Telecommunication Indicators questionnaires or from official information available on the Ministry or Regulator's website.
  • Mobile cellular subscriptions (per 100 people) indicator is derived by all mobile subscriptions divided by the country's population and multiplied by 100. For additional/latest information on sources and country notes, please also refer to: https://www.itu.int/en/ITU-D/Statistics/Pages/stat/default.aspx Statistical concept(s): Data can be collected from all licensed mobile-cellular operators in the country, and then aggregated at the country level.
  • A number of countries have fiscal years that end in March or June of every year. Data are usually not adjusted but discrepancies in the definition, reference year or the break in comparability in between years are noted in a data note. For this reason, data are not always strictly comparable. Missing values are estimated by ITU. Mobile subscriptions include both analogue and digital cellular systems (IMT-2000 (Third Generation, 3G) and 4G subscriptions, but excludes mobile broadband subscriptions via data cards or USB modems.

  • subscribers per 100 inhabitants in 1990 to 46.42 in 2004. The most rapid growth occurred in use of mobile · phones. From just 11 million subscribers in 1990, the number of mobile cellular subscribers grew to 1.8
  • The estimated number of personal computers (PCs) rose from some 120 million in 1990 to 777 million in · 2004. Worldwide, PC penetration (PCs per 100 people) stood at 13 at the end of 2004.
  • there are only three fixed lines for 100 Africans, the rate is even lower in Sub-Sahara Africa, where it stands · at 1.6 to one hundred. As a whole, developing countries now account for 58 per cent of all telephone · subscribers in the world, up from just 19 per cent in 1990.

message 0 | role=system | 7,099 chars
<system_instructions>
You are an assistant that answers factual questions using web search.

You have access to the following tools:

- `search_web`: Accepts a query string. Returns a list of results, each containing a title, URL, and snippet.
- `fetch_page`: Accepts a URL obtained from prior `search_web` results. Returns the extracted page text and fetch metadata.

<constraints>
- Every final answer must be grounded in evidence retrieved via `search_web` or `fetch_page`. Never answer from parametric knowledge alone.
- If multiple credible sources conflict, prefer the most recent, most authoritative source (official/government sites > news outlets > blogs/forums).
- If the question is time-sensitive (e.g., "current," "now," "latest," "as of"), prioritize the most recent source and note the date of the evidence in your reasoning.
</constraints>

<workflow>
1. **Understand the query.** Identify the core information need, any temporal constraints, and whether the question is single-part or multi-part. If multi-part, plan separate searches for each sub-question.
2. **Formulate search queries.** Write concise, keyword-focused queries. Avoid copying the user's question verbatim when a shorter, more targeted query would retrieve better results. You may issue multiple `search_web` calls in a single turn to fan out across sub-questions or alternative phrasings.
3. **Evaluate search results.** Check whether the snippets directly and unambiguously answer the question.
4. **Fetch when needed.** If snippets are insufficient, ambiguous, conflicting, or stale, use `fetch_page` on the most promising URLs. Prefer pages likely to contain direct evidence (official pages, primary sources, structured data). If the fetched content is still insufficient, reformulate your query and search again.
5. **Iterate if necessary.** If results remain inadequate, you are allowed to perform searches and fetches as you need.
6. **Produce the final answer.** Once you have sufficient evidence, output your answer following the output format rules.
</workflow>

<output_format>
- Prefix every final answer with `FINAL ANSWER: ` (exactly, including the trailing space).
- Return only the factual answer after the prefix — no reasoning, no source citations, no hedging language.
- Match the expected granularity: if the answer is a name, date, number, title, or short phrase, return only that value. If the question asks for a list, return a concise comma-separated list.
- If you cannot determine the answer after exhausting available retrieval actions, respond exactly: `FINAL ANSWER: I cannot determine the answer from available sources.`
</output_format>

<input_format>
- The user's question appears inside `<user_query>` tags.
- Search results appear inside `<search_documents>` tags.
- Fetched page contents appear inside `<fetched_page>` tags.
</input_format>
</system_instructions>

It is not a recommendation to always search, always fetch, or always abstain.
</purpose>

35th edition
The Yearbook of Statistics 2009 features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries, telecommunication regulatory authorities and national statistics offices. As such, the ITU Yearbook of Statistics provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the telecommunication sector, the availability of ICTs in households and the usage of ICTs by individuals.
The main features of this edition are:
- Presentation of data in country economy tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services by economy. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1999-2008. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a table are shown below.
- Inclusion of the latest telecommunication and ICT household statistics tables for some 190 economies worldwide.
- The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database available in the WIN*STARS v5.0 (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
English Edition (paper and on-line)
|
Price : 74 CHF - Order now ! |

28th edition
The Yearbook of Statistics (previously the &quot;Yearbook of Common Carrier Telecommunication Statistics&quot; or &quot;ITU Statistical Yearbook&quot;) features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities. As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide.
The main features of this edition are: Presentation of data in country tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services in a country. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period
1991-2000. The list of statistics (see below)
contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below.
Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s communication sector.
The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the
ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the STARS (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line),
French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

27th edition The 2001 Yearbook of Statistics (previously the &quot;Yearbook of Common Carrier Telecommunication Statistics&quot; or &quot;ITU Statistical Yearbook&quot;) features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities. As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide. The main features of this edition are: Presentation of data in country tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services in a country. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1990-1999. The list of statistics
(see below)
contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below.
Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s communication sector.
The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the
ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the STARS (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line),
French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

26th Edition
The 2000 Yearbook of Statistics (previously the &quot;Yearbook of Common Carrier Telecommunication Statistics&quot; or &quot;ITU Statistical Yearbook&quot;) features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities. As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide.
The main features of this edition are:
Presentation of data in country tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services in a country. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1989-1998. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below. Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s
sector.
The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the STARS (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line), French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

    <extra_snippet>The data are disseminated online, via CD Rom and through numerous ITU publications, including the Yearbook of Statistics and the Measuring the Information Society Report.     <extra_snippet>It includes time series for more than 140 indicators and around 200 economies.     <title>Mobile phone subscriptions per 100 people - Our World in Data</title>
    <url>https://ourworldindata.org/grapher/mobile-cellular-subscriptions-per-100-people</url>
    <domain>ourworldindata.org</domain>
    <snippet>Mobile cellular subscriptions (per 100 people) indicator is derived by all mobile subscriptions divided by the country&amp;#x27;s population and multiplied by 100. For additional/latest information on sources and country notes, please also refer to: https://www.itu.int/en/ITU-D/Statistics/Pages/stat/default.aspx Statistical concept(s): Data can be collected from all licensed mobile-cellular operators in the country, and then aggregated at the country level.</snippet>
    <extra_snippet>Data on mobile cellular subscribers are derived using administrative data that countries (usually the regulatory telecommunication authority or the Ministry in charge of telecommunications) regularly, and at least annually, collect from telecommunications operators. Data for this indicator are readily available for approximately 90 percent of countries, either through ITU&#x27;s World Telecommunication Indicators questionnaires or from official information available on the Ministry or Regulator&#x27;s website.</extra_snippet>
    <extra_snippet>Mobile cellular subscriptions (per 100 people) indicator is derived by all mobile subscriptions divided by the country&#x27;s population and multiplied by 100. For additional/latest information on sources and country notes, please also refer to: https://www.itu.int/en/ITU-D/Statistics/Pages/stat/default.aspx Statistical concept(s): Data can be collected from all licensed mobile-cellular operators in the country, and then aggregated at the country level.</extra_snippet>
    <extra_snippet>A number of countries have fiscal years that end in March or June of every year. Data are usually not adjusted but discrepancies in the definition, reference year or the break in comparability in between years are noted in a data note. For this reason, data are not always strictly comparable. Missing values are estimated by ITU. Mobile subscriptions include both analogue and digital cellular systems (IMT-2000 (Third Generation, 3G) and 4G subscriptions, but excludes mobile broadband subscriptions via data cards or USB modems.</extra_snippet>
    <extra_snippet>Subscriptions to public mobile data services, private trunked mobile radio, telepoint or radio paging, and telemetry services are also excluded, but all mobile cellular subscriptions that offer voice communications are included. Both postpaid and prepaid subscriptions are included. Please cite the International Telecommunication Union for third-party use of these data. ... International Telecommunication Union (ITU), via World Bank (2026) – processed by Our World in Data</extra_snippet>

Source
World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database
Source:
International Telecommunications Union
ITU's World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database is the main source of global, and internationally comparable, telecommunication/ICT statistics. It includes time series for more than 140 indicators and around 200 economies. The data are collected directly from telecommunication regulatory agencies and/or ministries and national statistical offices by means of an annual questionnaire, and subsequently verified, harmonized and complemented by ITU.
The data are disseminated online, via CD Rom and through numerous ITU publications, including the Yearbook of Statistics and the Measuring the Information Society Report. The statistics are used to track and benchmark the Information Society, to monitor the digital divide and to identify market potential and investment opportunities. They are an indispensable tool for policy makers in the area of ICT for development.
Download the footnotes in Excel format

message 0 | role=system | 7,099 chars
<system_instructions>
You are an assistant that answers factual questions using web search.

You have access to the following tools:

- `search_web`: Accepts a query string. Returns a list of results, each containing a title, URL, and snippet.
- `fetch_page`: Accepts a URL obtained from prior `search_web` results. Returns the extracted page text and fetch metadata.

<constraints>
- Every final answer must be grounded in evidence retrieved via `search_web` or `fetch_page`. Never answer from parametric knowledge alone.
- If multiple credible sources conflict, prefer the most recent, most authoritative source (official/government sites > news outlets > blogs/forums).
- If the question is time-sensitive (e.g., "current," "now," "latest," "as of"), prioritize the most recent source and note the date of the evidence in your reasoning.
</constraints>

<workflow>
1. **Understand the query.** Identify the core information need, any temporal constraints, and whether the question is single-part or multi-part. If multi-part, plan separate searches for each sub-question.
2. **Formulate search queries.** Write concise, keyword-focused queries. Avoid copying the user's question verbatim when a shorter, more targeted query would retrieve better results. You may issue multiple `search_web` calls in a single turn to fan out across sub-questions or alternative phrasings.
3. **Evaluate search results.** Check whether the snippets directly and unambiguously answer the question.
4. **Fetch when needed.** If snippets are insufficient, ambiguous, conflicting, or stale, use `fetch_page` on the most promising URLs. Prefer pages likely to contain direct evidence (official pages, primary sources, structured data). If the fetched content is still insufficient, reformulate your query and search again.
5. **Iterate if necessary.** If results remain inadequate, you are allowed to perform searches and fetches as you need.
6. **Produce the final answer.** Once you have sufficient evidence, output your answer following the output format rules.
</workflow>

<output_format>
- Prefix every final answer with `FINAL ANSWER: ` (exactly, including the trailing space).
- Return only the factual answer after the prefix — no reasoning, no source citations, no hedging language.
- Match the expected granularity: if the answer is a name, date, number, title, or short phrase, return only that value. If the question asks for a list, return a concise comma-separated list.
- If you cannot determine the answer after exhausting available retrieval actions, respond exactly: `FINAL ANSWER: I cannot determine the answer from available sources.`
</output_format>

<input_format>
- The user's question appears inside `<user_query>` tags.
- Search results appear inside `<search_documents>` tags.
- Fetched page contents appear inside `<fetched_page>` tags.
</input_format>
</system_instructions>

35th edition
The Yearbook of Statistics 2009 features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries, telecommunication regulatory authorities and national statistics offices. As such, the ITU Yearbook of Statistics provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the telecommunication sector, the availability of ICTs in households and the usage of ICTs by individuals.
The main features of this edition are:
- Presentation of data in country economy tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services by economy. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1999-2008. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a table are shown below.
- Inclusion of the latest telecommunication and ICT household statistics tables for some 190 economies worldwide.
- The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database available in the WIN*STARS v5.0 (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
English Edition (paper and on-line)

32nd edition The Yearbook of Statistics
2006 features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to
telecommunication/ICT ministries, telecommunication regulatory authorities and
national statistics offices. As such, the ITU Yearbook of Statistics provides
the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the
telecommunication sector, the availability of ICTs in households and the usage of ICTs by individuals. The main features of this edition are:
- Presentation of data in country economy tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services by economy. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1995-2004. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a table are shown below.
- Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s communication sector.
- The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the WIN*STARS v5.0 (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line), French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

The Yearbook of Statistics 2005 features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities, as well as data obtained from national statistics offices. As such, the ITU Yearbook of Statistics provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the telecommunication sector. It also includes a limited amount of data on ICTs in households and the usage of ICTs by individuals.
The main features of this edition are:

28th edition
The Yearbook of Statistics (previously the &quot;Yearbook of Common Carrier Telecommunication Statistics&quot; or &quot;ITU Statistical Yearbook&quot;) features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities. As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide.
The main features of this edition are: Presentation of data in country tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services in a country. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period
1991-2000. The list of statistics (see below)
contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below.

27th edition The 2001 Yearbook of Statistics (previously the &quot;Yearbook of Common Carrier Telecommunication Statistics&quot; or &quot;ITU Statistical Yearbook&quot;) features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities. As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide. The main features of this edition are: Presentation of data in country tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services in a country. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1990-1999. The list of statistics
(see below)
contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below.
Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s communication sector.
The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the
ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the STARS (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line),
French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

26th Edition
The 2000 Yearbook of Statistics (previously the &quot;Yearbook of Common Carrier Telecommunication Statistics&quot; or &quot;ITU Statistical Yearbook&quot;) features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities. As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide.
The main features of this edition are:
Presentation of data in country tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services in a country. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1989-1998. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below. Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s
sector.
The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the STARS (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line), French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

    <snippet>Mobile cellular subscriptions (per 100 people) indicator is derived by all mobile subscriptions divided by the country&amp;#x27;s population and multiplied by 100. For additional/latest information on sources and country notes, please also refer to: https://www.itu.int/en/ITU-D/Statistics/Pages/stat/default.aspx Statistical concept(s): Data can be collected from all licensed mobile-cellular operators in the country, and then aggregated at the country level.</snippet>
    <extra_snippet>Data on mobile cellular subscribers are derived using administrative data that countries (usually the regulatory telecommunication authority or the Ministry in charge of telecommunications) regularly, and at least annually, collect from telecommunications operators. Data for this indicator are readily available for approximately 90 percent of countries, either through ITU&#x27;s World Telecommunication Indicators questionnaires or from official information available on the Ministry or Regulator&#x27;s website.</extra_snippet>
    <extra_snippet>Mobile cellular subscriptions (per 100 people) indicator is derived by all mobile subscriptions divided by the country&#x27;s population and multiplied by 100. For additional/latest information on sources and country notes, please also refer to: https://www.itu.int/en/ITU-D/Statistics/Pages/stat/default.aspx Statistical concept(s): Data can be collected from all licensed mobile-cellular operators in the country, and then aggregated at the country level.</extra_snippet>
    <extra_snippet>A number of countries have fiscal years that end in March or June of every year. Data are usually not adjusted but discrepancies in the definition, reference year or the break in comparability in between years are noted in a data note. For this reason, data are not always strictly comparable. Missing values are estimated by ITU. Mobile subscriptions include both analogue and digital cellular systems (IMT-2000 (Third Generation, 3G) and 4G subscriptions, but excludes mobile broadband subscriptions via data cards or USB modems.</extra_snippet>
    <extra_snippet>Subscriptions to public mobile data services, private trunked mobile radio, telepoint or radio paging, and telemetry services are also excluded, but all mobile cellular subscriptions that offer voice communications are included. Both postpaid and prepaid subscriptions are included. Please cite the International Telecommunication Union for third-party use of these data. ... International Telecommunication Union (ITU), via World Bank (2026) – processed by Our World in Data</extra_snippet>

Source
World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database
Source:
International Telecommunications Union
ITU&#x27;s World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database is the main source of global, and internationally comparable, telecommunication/ICT statistics. It includes time series for more than 140 indicators and around 200 economies. The data are collected directly from telecommunication regulatory agencies and/or ministries and national statistical offices by means of an annual questionnaire, and subsequently verified, harmonized and complemented by ITU.
The data are disseminated online, via CD Rom and through numerous ITU publications, including the Yearbook of Statistics and the Measuring the Information Society Report. The statistics are used to track and benchmark the Information Society, to monitor the digital divide and to identify market potential and investment opportunities. They are an indispensable tool for policy makers in the area of ICT for development.
Download the footnotes in Excel format

#1

UNdata | api manual

https://data.un.org/Host.aspx?Content=API
data.un.org

To use UNdata API, you first need to create an SDMX Query. This is an XML document that defines query parameters in accordance with the dataset you intend to retrieve. Queries can be easily created with SDMX Browser.

extra snippets (4)
  • If you want to query data from UNData API we have two options for you. You can use REST API or the SOAP web service. In any of these cases it is recommended that you get familiarized with the main SDMX artifacts such as DataFlow, Codelist, Agency, Structure, etc.
  • To use UNdata API, you first need to create an SDMX Query. This is an XML document that defines query parameters in accordance with the dataset you intend to retrieve. Queries can be easily created with SDMX Browser.
  • To be exposed through SDMX API, each datamart requires an SDMX Data Structure Definition (DSD). We are in the process of mapping UNdata datamarts to available DSDs, as well as developing new DSD where required.

#10

Memahami Struktur Data V.2.0.0 (Sorting) | by GDSC Universitas Mulia | Medium

https://gdscuniversitasmulia.medium.com/memahami-struktur-data-v-2-0-0-sorting-9d311b309a56
gdscuniversitasmulia.medium.com

Bagian yang belum diurutkan akan dimasukan ke bagian yang sudah diurutkan sesuai urutan yang Kita inginkan, oleh karena itu algoritma ini dinamakan Insertion Sort. Contoh Kita punya array dengan data seperti berikut : Insertion sort dimulai dari dua index pertama untuk membandingkan sesuai dengan urutan yang Kita inginkan ascending atau descending.

extra snippets (4)
  • Bagian yang belum diurutkan akan dimasukan ke bagian yang sudah diurutkan sesuai urutan yang Kita inginkan, oleh karena itu algoritma ini dinamakan Insertion Sort. Contoh Kita punya array dengan data seperti berikut : Insertion sort dimulai dari dua index pertama untuk membandingkan sesuai dengan urutan yang Kita inginkan ascending atau descending.
  • Stabilitas sebuah algoritma itu penting ketika kita memiliki data key-value dengan kemungkinan terdapat key yang sama (seperti nama orang sebagai key dan detailnya sebagai value). Dan Kita ingin mengurutkan data tersebut berdasarkan key.
  • Algoritma yang tidak membutuhkan extra space, yang hanya terjadi di dalam array itu sendiri dinamakan In-place sorting.

message 0 | role=system | 7,099 chars
<system_instructions>
You are an assistant that answers factual questions using web search.

You have access to the following tools:

- `search_web`: Accepts a query string. Returns a list of results, each containing a title, URL, and snippet.
- `fetch_page`: Accepts a URL obtained from prior `search_web` results. Returns the extracted page text and fetch metadata.

<constraints>
- Every final answer must be grounded in evidence retrieved via `search_web` or `fetch_page`. Never answer from parametric knowledge alone.
- If multiple credible sources conflict, prefer the most recent, most authoritative source (official/government sites > news outlets > blogs/forums).
- If the question is time-sensitive (e.g., "current," "now," "latest," "as of"), prioritize the most recent source and note the date of the evidence in your reasoning.
</constraints>

<workflow>
1. **Understand the query.** Identify the core information need, any temporal constraints, and whether the question is single-part or multi-part. If multi-part, plan separate searches for each sub-question.
2. **Formulate search queries.** Write concise, keyword-focused queries. Avoid copying the user's question verbatim when a shorter, more targeted query would retrieve better results. You may issue multiple `search_web` calls in a single turn to fan out across sub-questions or alternative phrasings.
3. **Evaluate search results.** Check whether the snippets directly and unambiguously answer the question.
4. **Fetch when needed.** If snippets are insufficient, ambiguous, conflicting, or stale, use `fetch_page` on the most promising URLs. Prefer pages likely to contain direct evidence (official pages, primary sources, structured data). If the fetched content is still insufficient, reformulate your query and search again.
5. **Iterate if necessary.** If results remain inadequate, you are allowed to perform searches and fetches as you need.
6. **Produce the final answer.** Once you have sufficient evidence, output your answer following the output format rules.
</workflow>

<output_format>
- Prefix every final answer with `FINAL ANSWER: ` (exactly, including the trailing space).
- Return only the factual answer after the prefix — no reasoning, no source citations, no hedging language.
- Match the expected granularity: if the answer is a name, date, number, title, or short phrase, return only that value. If the question asks for a list, return a concise comma-separated list.
- If you cannot determine the answer after exhausting available retrieval actions, respond exactly: `FINAL ANSWER: I cannot determine the answer from available sources.`
</output_format>

<input_format>
- The user's question appears inside `<user_query>` tags.
- Search results appear inside `<search_documents>` tags.
- Fetched page contents appear inside `<fetched_page>` tags.
</input_format>
</system_instructions>

<example name="neutral_evidence_use">
<purpose>
This example demonstrates the complete retrieval workflow: formulating a search, evaluating snippets, fetching a page when snippets are insufficient, and producing a grounded final answer.
It is not a recommendation to always search, always fetch, or always abstain.
</purpose>

<system_instructions_example>
You are answering a factual question. Use search_web to find evidence and fetch_page when snippets are insufficient.
Answer only when the retrieved documents support the answer.
</system_instructions_example>

<user_query_example>
How many mass drivers does the Aegis Avenger Titan come equipped with in Star Citizen?
</user_query_example>

The Aegis Avenger Titan is a light freight/combat ship manufactured by Aegis Dynamics.

Default Loadout:
- Nose: 1x S3 M5A Laser Cannon
- Wings: 2x S2 Bulldog Repeaters

Hardpoints:
- 1x S3 nose gimbal mount
- 2x S2 wing gimbal mounts

</turn_3>

<decision_guidance_example>
This example illustrates three key decisions:
1. **Search first**: The question involves specific game data that requires retrieval.
2. **Fetch when snippets are vague**: Snippets mentioned weapons but not mass drivers specifically, so fetch_page was used to get the full loadout details.
3. **Answer what the evidence shows**: The evidence contradicted the premise of the question. The correct response is to state what the evidence supports, not to force-fit an answer to match the question's assumption.

If the fetched page also lacked loadout details, the next step would be to search again with a reformulated query (e.g., "Avenger Titan default weapons list site:starcitizen.tools").
If no source could confirm the loadout after multiple attempts, the correct response would be: `FINAL ANSWER: I cannot determine the answer from available sources.`
</decision_guidance_example>

35th edition
The Yearbook of Statistics 2009 features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries, telecommunication regulatory authorities and national statistics offices. As such, the ITU Yearbook of Statistics provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the telecommunication sector, the availability of ICTs in households and the usage of ICTs by individuals.
The main features of this edition are:
- Presentation of data in country economy tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services by economy. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1999-2008. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a table are shown below.
- Inclusion of the latest telecommunication and ICT household statistics tables for some 190 economies worldwide.
- The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database available in the WIN*STARS v5.0 (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).

32nd edition The Yearbook of Statistics
2006 features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to
telecommunication/ICT ministries, telecommunication regulatory authorities and
national statistics offices. As such, the ITU Yearbook of Statistics provides
the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the
telecommunication sector, the availability of ICTs in households and the usage of ICTs by individuals. The main features of this edition are:
- Presentation of data in country economy tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services by economy. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1995-2004. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a table are shown below.
- Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s communication sector.
- The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the WIN*STARS v5.0 (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line), French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s
sector.
The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the STARS (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line), French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

    <extra_snippet>Data on mobile cellular subscribers are derived using administrative data that countries (usually the regulatory telecommunication authority or the Ministry in charge of telecommunications) regularly, and at least annually, collect from telecommunications operators. Data for this indicator are readily available for approximately 90 percent of countries, either through ITU&#x27;s World Telecommunication Indicators questionnaires or from official information available on the Ministry or Regulator&#x27;s website.</extra_snippet>
    <extra_snippet>Mobile cellular subscriptions (per 100 people) indicator is derived by all mobile subscriptions divided by the country&#x27;s population and multiplied by 100. For additional/latest information on sources and country notes, please also refer to: https://www.itu.int/en/ITU-D/Statistics/Pages/stat/default.aspx Statistical concept(s): Data can be collected from all licensed mobile-cellular operators in the country, and then aggregated at the country level.</extra_snippet>
    <extra_snippet>A number of countries have fiscal years that end in March or June of every year. Data are usually not adjusted but discrepancies in the definition, reference year or the break in comparability in between years are noted in a data note. For this reason, data are not always strictly comparable. Missing values are estimated by ITU. Mobile subscriptions include both analogue and digital cellular systems (IMT-2000 (Third Generation, 3G) and 4G subscriptions, but excludes mobile broadband subscriptions via data cards or USB modems.</extra_snippet>
    <extra_snippet>Subscriptions to public mobile data services, private trunked mobile radio, telepoint or radio paging, and telemetry services are also excluded, but all mobile cellular subscriptions that offer voice communications are included. Source
World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database
Source:
International Telecommunications Union
ITU&#x27;s World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database is the main source of global, and internationally comparable, telecommunication/ICT statistics. It includes time series for more than 140 indicators and around 200 economies. The data are collected directly from telecommunication regulatory agencies and/or ministries and national statistical offices by means of an annual questionnaire, and subsequently verified, harmonized and complemented by ITU.
The data are disseminated online, via CD Rom and through numerous ITU publications, including the Yearbook of Statistics and the Measuring the Information Society Report. The statistics are used to track and benchmark the Information Society, to monitor the digital divide and to identify market potential and investment opportunities. They are an indispensable tool for policy makers in the area of ICT for development.
Download the footnotes in Excel format

    <title>UNdata | api manual</title>
    <url>https://data.un.org/Host.aspx?Content=API</url>
    <domain>data.un.org</domain>
    <snippet>To use UNdata API, you first need to create an SDMX Query. This is an XML document that defines query parameters in accordance with the dataset you intend to retrieve. Queries can be easily created with SDMX Browser.</snippet>
    <extra_snippet>If you want to query data from UNData API we have two options for you. You can use REST API or the SOAP web service. In any of these cases it is recommended that you get familiarized with the main SDMX artifacts such as DataFlow, Codelist, Agency, Structure, etc.</extra_snippet>
    <extra_snippet>To use UNdata API, you first need to create an SDMX Query. This is an XML document that defines query parameters in accordance with the dataset you intend to retrieve. Queries can be easily created with SDMX Browser.</extra_snippet>
    <extra_snippet>To be exposed through SDMX API, each datamart requires an SDMX Data Structure Definition (DSD). We are in the process of mapping UNdata datamarts to available DSDs, as well as developing new DSD where required.</extra_snippet>
    <extra_snippet>In SDMX, dataset structure and codes are defined prior to data exchange, just like a relational database structure needs to be defined before the database can be used. These structures are stored in a document called Data Structure Definition (DSD). To establish data dissemination, each UNdata datamart requires one or more DSDs which, as much as possible, should be internationally standardized.</extra_snippet>

<system_instructions>
You are an assistant that answers factual questions using web search.

You have access to the following tools:

- `search_web`: Accepts a query string. Returns a list of results, each containing a title, URL, and snippet.
- `fetch_page`: Accepts a URL obtained from prior `search_web` results. Returns the extracted page text and fetch metadata.

<constraints>
- Every final answer must be grounded in evidence retrieved via `search_web` or `fetch_page`. Never answer from parametric knowledge alone.
- If multiple credible sources conflict, prefer the most recent, most authoritative source (official/government sites > news outlets > blogs/forums).
- If the question is time-sensitive (e.g., "current," "now," "latest," "as of"), prioritize the most recent source and note the date of the evidence in your reasoning.
</constraints>

<workflow>
1. **Understand the query.** Identify the core information need, any temporal constraints, and whether the question is single-part or multi-part. If multi-part, plan separate searches for each sub-question.
2. **Formulate search queries.** Write concise, keyword-focused queries. Avoid copying the user's question verbatim when a shorter, more targeted query would retrieve better results. You may issue multiple `search_web` calls in a single turn to fan out across sub-questions or alternative phrasings.
3. **Evaluate search results.** Check whether the snippets directly and unambiguously answer the question.
4. **Fetch when needed.** If snippets are insufficient, ambiguous, conflicting, or stale, use `fetch_page` on the most promising URLs. Prefer pages likely to contain direct evidence (official pages, primary sources, structured data). If the fetched content is still insufficient, reformulate your query and search again.
5. **Iterate if necessary.** If results remain inadequate, you are allowed to perform searches and fetches as you need.
6. **Produce the final answer.** Once you have sufficient evidence, output your answer following the output format rules.
</workflow>

<output_format>
- Prefix every final answer with `FINAL ANSWER: ` (exactly, including the trailing space).
- Return only the factual answer after the prefix — no reasoning, no source citations, no hedging language.
- Match the expected granularity: if the answer is a name, date, number, title, or short phrase, return only that value. If the question asks for a list, return a concise comma-separated list.
- If you cannot determine the answer after exhausting available retrieval actions, respond exactly: `FINAL ANSWER: I cannot determine the answer from available sources.`
</output_format>

<input_format>
- The user's question appears inside `<user_query>` tags.
- Search results appear inside `<search_documents>` tags.
- Fetched page contents appear inside `<fetched_page>` tags.
</input_format>
</system_instructions>

35th edition
The Yearbook of Statistics 2009 features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries, telecommunication regulatory authorities and national statistics offices. As such, the ITU Yearbook of Statistics provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the telecommunication sector, the availability of ICTs in households and the usage of ICTs by individuals.
The main features of this edition are:
- Presentation of data in country economy tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services by economy. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1999-2008. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a table are shown below.
- Inclusion of the latest telecommunication and ICT household statistics tables for some 190 economies worldwide.
- The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication/ICT Indicators Database available in the WIN*STARS v5.0 (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).

32nd edition The Yearbook of Statistics
2006 features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to
telecommunication/ICT ministries, telecommunication regulatory authorities and
national statistics offices. As such, the ITU Yearbook of Statistics provides
the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the
telecommunication sector, the availability of ICTs in households and the usage of ICTs by individuals. The main features of this edition are:
- Presentation of data in country economy tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services by economy. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1995-2004. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a table are shown below.
- Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s communication sector.
- The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the WIN*STARS v5.0 (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).

As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide.

1991-2000. The list of statistics (see below)
contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below.

27th edition The 2001 Yearbook of Statistics (previously the &quot;Yearbook of Common Carrier Telecommunication Statistics&quot; or &quot;ITU Statistical Yearbook&quot;) features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities. As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide. The main features of this edition are: Presentation of data in country tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services in a country. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1990-1999. The list of statistics
(see below)
contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below.
Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s communication sector.
The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the
ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the STARS (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line),
French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

26th Edition
The 2000 Yearbook of Statistics (previously the &quot;Yearbook of Common Carrier Telecommunication Statistics&quot; or &quot;ITU Statistical Yearbook&quot;) features data collected and processed by ITU through questionnaires sent to telecommunication/ICT ministries and telecommunication regulatory authorities. As such, the ITU Yearbook provides the most authoritative source of data about the evolution of the public telecommunication services sector available worldwide.
The main features of this edition are:
Presentation of data in country tables allowing readers to view the evolution of telecommunication services in a country. Statistics are provided for the ten-year period 1989-1998. The list of statistics (see below) contained in the Yearbook and the economies (see below) for which there is a page is shown below. Inclusion of selected television broadcasting and information technology time series to provide a wider picture of a country&#x27;s
sector.
The Yearbook is available in electronic form in Adobe Acrobat (PDF). The data shown in the Yearbook are also contained in the ITU World Telecommunication Indicators Database available in the STARS (Socio-economic Time series Access and Retrieval System) data retrieval format, which permits easy selection of the required data and conversion to spreadsheets or ASCII text (requires use of IBM-PC compatible computer).
Separate editions in English (paper and on-line), French (on-line) and Spanish (on-line)

    <extra_snippet>The data are disseminated online, via CD Rom and through numerous ITU publications, including the Yearbook of Statistics and the Measuring the Information Society Report.
